         November 20, 1969, 17:58:20 UTC
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Undocking date
        </th>
        <td>
         November 20, 1969, 20:21:31 UTC
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="display:none">
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <p>
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_insignia.png">
           <img alt="Apollo 12 insignia.png" data-file-height="3340" data-file-width="3340" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Apollo_12_insignia.png/180px-Apollo_12_insignia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Apollo_12_insignia.png/270px-Apollo_12_insignia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Apollo_12_insignia.png/360px-Apollo_12_insignia.png 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_crew.jpg">
          <img alt="Apollo 12 crew.jpg" data-file-height="2263" data-file-width="4000" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Apollo_12_crew.jpg/220px-Apollo_12_crew.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Apollo_12_crew.jpg/330px-Apollo_12_crew.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Apollo_12_crew.jpg/440px-Apollo_12_crew.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
         </a>
         <br/>
         Left to right: Conrad, Gordon, Bean
         <div class="" style="width:100%; text-align:center; border-top:1px #aaa solid">
          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
           Apollo program
          </a>
         </div>
         <div style="width:100%">
          <div class="noprint" style="float: left; text-align:left;padding-right:0.5em;">
           ←
           <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
            Apollo 11
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="noprint" style="float: right; text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">
            Apollo 13
           </a>
           →
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Apollo 12
       </b>
       was the sixth manned flight in the United States
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
        Apollo program
       </a>
       and the second to land on the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       . It was launched on November 14, 1969, from the
       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">
        Kennedy Space Center
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">
        Florida
       </a>
       , four months after
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
        Apollo 11
       </a>
       . Mission commander
       <a href="/wiki/Pete_Conrad" title="Pete Conrad">
        Charles "Pete" Conrad
       </a>
       and Lunar Module Pilot
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bean" title="Alan Bean">
        Alan L. Bean
       </a>
       performed just over one day and seven hours of lunar surface activity while Command Module Pilot
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_F._Gordon_Jr." title="Richard F. Gordon Jr.">
        Richard F. Gordon
       </a>
       remained in lunar orbit. The landing site for the mission was located in the southeastern portion of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocean_of_Storms" title="Ocean of Storms">
        Ocean of Storms
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Unlike the first landing on Apollo 11, Conrad and Bean achieved a precise landing at their expected location, the site of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Surveyor_3" title="Surveyor 3">
         Surveyor 3
        </a>
       </i>
       unmanned probe, which had landed on April 20, 1967. They carried the first color television camera to the lunar surface on an Apollo flight, but transmission was lost after Bean accidentally destroyed the camera by pointing it at the Sun. On one of two moonwalks, they visited the
       <i>
        Surveyor
       </i>
       and removed some parts for return to Earth. The mission ended on November 24 with a successful
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Splashdown_(spacecraft_landing)" title="Splashdown (spacecraft landing)">
        splashdown
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h4>

        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: EVA 2 start: November 20, 1969, 03:54:45 UTC">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         Conrad
        </i>
        — EVA 2
       </li>

        </b>

       </li>

       </li>

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table style="float: right">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_and_transfer">
        Launch and transfer
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Launch and transfer">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_launches_from_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4324" data-file-width="4324" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Apollo_12_launches_from_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg/220px-Apollo_12_launches_from_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Apollo_12_launches_from_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg/330px-Apollo_12_launches_from_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Apollo_12_launches_from_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg/440px-Apollo_12_launches_from_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_launches_from_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo 12 launches from Kennedy Space Center, November 14, 1969
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Apollo 12 launched on schedule from Kennedy Space Center, during a rainstorm. It was the first rocket launch attended by an incumbent US president,
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
        Richard Nixon
       </a>
       . Thirty-six-and-a-half seconds after lift-off, the vehicle triggered a
       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">
        lightning
       </a>
       discharge through itself and down to the Earth through the Saturn's ionized plume. Protective circuits on the
       <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">
        fuel cells
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module#Service_Module_(SM)" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">
        Service Module
       </a>
       (SM) falsely detected overloads and took all three fuel cells offline, along with much of the Command/Service Module (CSM) instrumentation. A second strike at 52 seconds after launch knocked out the "8-ball"
       <a href="/wiki/Attitude_indicator" title="Attitude indicator">
        attitude indicator
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Telemetry" title="Telemetry">
        telemetry
       </a>
       stream at
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center#Houston_(1965–present)" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">
        Mission Control
       </a>
       was garbled. However, the vehicle continued to fly correctly; the strikes had not affected the
       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V_Instrument_Unit" title="Saturn V Instrument Unit">
        Saturn V Instrument Unit
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The loss of all three fuel cells put the CSM entirely on batteries, which were unable to maintain normal 75-ampere launch loads on the 28-volt DC bus. One of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inverter_(electrical)" title="Inverter (electrical)">
        AC inverters
       </a>
       dropped offline. These power supply problems lit nearly every warning light on the control panel and caused much of the instrumentation to malfunction.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Flight_controller#Electrical,_Environmental_and_Consumables_Manager_(EECOM)" title="Flight controller">
        Electrical, Environmental and Consumables Manager (EECOM)
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/John_Aaron" title="John Aaron">
        John Aaron
       </a>
       remembered the telemetry failure pattern from an earlier test when a power supply malfunctioned in the CSM Signal Conditioning Electronics (SCE), which converted raw signals from instrumentation to standard voltages for the spacecraft instrument displays and telemetry encoders.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aaron made a call, "Try SCE to aux," which switched the SCE to a backup power supply. The switch was fairly obscure, and neither
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight_Director" title="Flight Director">
        Flight Director
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Gerald_D._Griffin" title="Gerald D. Griffin">
        Gerald Griffin
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capsule_communicator" title="Capsule communicator">
        CAPCOM
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Gerald_P._Carr" title="Gerald P. Carr">
        Gerald Carr
       </a>
       , nor Mission Commander Pete Conrad immediately recognized it. Lunar Module Pilot Alan Bean, flying in the right seat as the spacecraft systems engineer, remembered the SCE switch from a training incident a year earlier when the same failure had been
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simulated" title="Simulated">
        simulated
       </a>
       . Aaron's quick thinking and Bean's memory saved what could have been an
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_abort_modes" title="Apollo abort modes">
        aborted mission
       </a>
       , and earned Aaron the reputation of a "steely-eyed missile man".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lost_Moon_1994_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lost_Moon_1994-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bean put the fuel cells back on line, and with telemetry restored, the launch continued successfully. Once in Earth
       <a href="/wiki/Parking_orbit" title="Parking orbit">
        parking orbit
       </a>
       , the crew carefully checked out their spacecraft before re-igniting the
       <a href="/wiki/S-IVB" title="S-IVB">
        S-IVB
       </a>
       third stage for
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-lunar_injection" title="Trans-lunar injection">
        trans-lunar injection
       </a>
       . The lightning strikes had caused no serious permanent damage.
      </p>
      <p>
       Initially, it was feared that the lightning strike could have caused the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module#Command_Module_(CM)" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">
        Command Module
       </a>
       's (CM) parachute mechanism to prematurely fire, disabling the explosive bolts that open the parachute compartment to deploy them.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       If they were indeed disabled, the Command Module would have crashed uncontrollably into the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       and killed the crew instantly. Since there was no way to figure out whether or not this was the case, ground controllers decided not to tell the astronauts about the possibility. The parachutes deployed and functioned normally at the end of the mission.
      </p>
      <p>
       After
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module" title="Apollo Lunar Module">
        Lunar Module
       </a>
       (LM) separation, the S-IVB was intended to fly into solar orbit. The S-IVB auxiliary propulsion system was fired, and the remaining propellants vented to slow it down to fly past the Moon's trailing edge (the Apollo spacecraft always approached the Moon's leading edge). The Moon's gravity would then slingshot the stage into solar orbit. However, a small error in the state vector in the Saturn's guidance system caused the S-IVB to fly past the Moon at too high an altitude to achieve Earth escape velocity. It remained in a semi-stable Earth orbit after passing the Moon on November 18, 1969. It finally escaped Earth orbit in 1971 but was briefly recaptured in Earth orbit 31 years later. It was discovered by amateur astronomer
       <a href="/wiki/William_Kwong_Yu_Yeung" title="William Kwong Yu Yeung">
        Bill Yeung
       </a>
       who gave it the temporary designation
       <a href="/wiki/J002E3" title="J002E3">
        J002E3
       </a>
       before it was determined to be an artificial object.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jorgensen_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jorgensen-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Moon_landing">
        Moon landing
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Moon landing">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4095" data-file-width="4074" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg/220px-Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg/330px-Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg/440px-Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Lunar Module above the Moon
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_landing_site_3154_h2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1800" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Apollo_12_landing_site_3154_h2.jpg/220px-Apollo_12_landing_site_3154_h2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Apollo_12_landing_site_3154_h2.jpg/330px-Apollo_12_landing_site_3154_h2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Apollo_12_landing_site_3154_h2.jpg/440px-Apollo_12_landing_site_3154_h2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_landing_site_3154_h2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         High-resolution
         <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Orbiter_3" title="Lunar Orbiter 3">
          Lunar Orbiter 3
         </a>
         image of the Apollo 12 landing site at center, used in mission planning. The area shown is approximately 1.75 x 1.75 km.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_landing_site_imaged_by_LRO,_2011.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Apollo_12_landing_site_imaged_by_LRO%2C_2011.jpg/220px-Apollo_12_landing_site_imaged_by_LRO%2C_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Apollo_12_landing_site_imaged_by_LRO%2C_2011.jpg/330px-Apollo_12_landing_site_imaged_by_LRO%2C_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Apollo_12_landing_site_imaged_by_LRO%2C_2011.jpg/440px-Apollo_12_landing_site_imaged_by_LRO%2C_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_landing_site_imaged_by_LRO,_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Landing site photographed by
         <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter">
          Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter
         </a>
         in 2011
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Apollo 12 mission landed on November 19, 1969, on an area of the Ocean of Storms (Latin
       <i>
        Oceanus Procellarum
       </i>
       ) that had been visited earlier by several unmanned missions (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Luna_5" title="Luna 5">
         Luna 5
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Surveyor_3" title="Surveyor 3">
         Surveyor 3
        </a>
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ranger_7" title="Ranger 7">
         Ranger 7
        </a>
       </i>
       ). The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">
        International Astronomical Union
       </a>
       , recognizing this, christened this region
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mare_Cognitum" title="Mare Cognitum">
         Mare Cognitum
        </a>
        (Known Sea)
       </i>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Selenographic_coordinates" title="Selenographic coordinates">
        Lunar coordinates
       </a>
       of the landing site were 3.01239° S latitude, 23.42157° W longitude.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The landing site would thereafter be listed as
       <i>
        Statio Cognitum
       </i>
       on lunar maps. Conrad and Bean did not formally name their landing site, though Conrad nicknamed the intended touchdown area "Pete's Parking Lot".
      </p>
      <p>
       The second lunar landing was an exercise in precision targeting, which would be needed for future Apollo missions. Most of the descent was automatic, with manual control assumed by Conrad during the final few hundred feet of descent. Unlike Apollo 11, where
       <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">
        Neil Armstrong
       </a>
       had to use the manual control to direct his lander downrange of the computer's target which was strewn with boulders, Apollo 12 succeeded in landing at its intended target – within walking distance of the
       <i>
        Surveyor 3
       </i>
       probe, which had landed on the Moon in April 1967.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaikin_1995_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chaikin_1995-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was the first – and, to date, only – occasion in which humans have "caught up" to a probe sent to land on another world.
      </p>
      <p>
       Conrad actually landed
       <i>
        Intrepid
       </i>
       580 feet (177 m) short of "Pete's Parking Lot", because it looked rougher during final approach than anticipated, and was a little under 1,180 feet (360 m) from
       <i>
        Surveyor 3
       </i>
       , a distance that was chosen to eliminate the possibility of lunar dust (being kicked up by
       <i>
        Intrepid's
       </i>
       descent engine during landing) from covering
       <i>
        Surveyor 3
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1969_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1969-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       But the actual touchdown point–approximately 600 feet (183 m) from
       <i>
        Surveyor 3
       </i>
       –did cause high velocity sandblasting of the probe. It was later determined that the sandblasting removed more dust than it delivered onto the
       <i>
        Surveyor
       </i>
       , because the probe was covered by a thin layer that gave it a tan hue as observed by the astronauts, and every portion of the surface exposed to the direct sandblasting was lightened back toward the original white color through the removal of lunar dust.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="EVAs">
        EVAs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: EVAs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       When Conrad, who was somewhat shorter than Neil Armstrong, stepped onto the lunar surface, his first words were "Whoopie! Man, that may have been a small one for Neil, but that's a long one for me."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaikin_1995_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chaikin_1995-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was not an off-the-cuff remark: Conrad had made a
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$500
       </span>
       bet with reporter
       <a href="/wiki/Oriana_Fallaci" title="Oriana Fallaci">
        Oriana Fallaci
       </a>
       he would say these words, after she had queried whether NASA had instructed Neil Armstrong what to say as he stepped onto the Moon. Conrad later said he was never able to collect the money.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       To improve the quality of television pictures from the Moon, a color camera was carried on Apollo 12 (unlike the monochrome camera that was used on Apollo 11). Unfortunately, when Bean carried the camera to the place near the Lunar Module where it was to be set up, he inadvertently pointed it directly into the Sun, destroying the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_TV_camera#Westinghouse_Lunar_Color_Camera" title="Apollo TV camera">
        Secondary Electron Conduction (SEC) tube
       </a>
       . Television coverage of this mission was thus terminated almost immediately.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_TV_camera" title="Apollo TV camera">
        Apollo TV camera
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Apollo 12 successfully landed within walking distance of the
       <a href="/wiki/Surveyor_3" title="Surveyor 3">
        Surveyor 3
       </a>
       probe. Conrad and Bean removed pieces of the probe to be taken back to Earth for analysis. It is claimed that the common
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterium" title="Bacterium">
        bacterium
       </a>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Streptococcus_mitis" title="Streptococcus mitis">
         Streptococcus mitis
        </a>
       </i>
       was found to have accidentally contaminated the spacecraft's camera prior to launch and survived dormant in this harsh environment for two and a half years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, this finding has since been disputed: see
       <a href="/wiki/Reports_of_Streptococcus_mitis_on_the_Moon" title="Reports of Streptococcus mitis on the Moon">
        Reports of
        <i>
         Streptococcus mitis
        </i>
        on the Moon
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Astronauts Conrad and Bean also collected rocks and set up equipment that took measurements of the Moon's
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_seismology" title="Lunar seismology">
        seismicity
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_wind" title="Solar wind">
        solar wind
       </a>
       flux and
       <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">
        magnetic field
       </a>
       , and relayed the measurements to Earth. The instruments were part of the first complete nuclear-powered
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Surface_Experiments_Package" title="Apollo Lunar Surface Experiments Package">
        ALSEP
       </a>
       station set up by astronauts on the Moon to relay long-term data from the lunar surface. The instruments on Apollo 11 were not as extensive or designed to operate long term. The astronauts also took photographs, although by accident Bean left several rolls of exposed film on the lunar surface. Meanwhile, Gordon, on board the
       <i>
        Yankee Clipper
       </i>
       in lunar orbit, took multi-spectral photographs of the surface.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_plaque" title="Lunar plaque">
        lunar plaque
       </a>
       attached to the descent stage of
       <i>
        Intrepid
       </i>
       is unique in that unlike the other plaques, it (a) did not have a depiction of the Earth, and (b) it was textured differently (the other plaques had black lettering on polished stainless steel while the Apollo 12 plaque had the lettering in polished stainless steel while the background was brushed flat).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Return">
        Return
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Return">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SH-3D_of_HS-4_flies_over_Apollo_12_command_module_near_USS_Hornet_(CVS-12)_on_24_November_1969.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="483" data-file-width="687" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/SH-3D_of_HS-4_flies_over_Apollo_12_command_module_near_USS_Hornet_%28CVS-12%29_on_24_November_1969.jpg/220px-SH-3D_of_HS-4_flies_over_Apollo_12_command_module_near_USS_Hornet_%28CVS-12%29_on_24_November_1969.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/SH-3D_of_HS-4_flies_over_Apollo_12_command_module_near_USS_Hornet_%28CVS-12%29_on_24_November_1969.jpg/330px-SH-3D_of_HS-4_flies_over_Apollo_12_command_module_near_USS_Hornet_%28CVS-12%29_on_24_November_1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/SH-3D_of_HS-4_flies_over_Apollo_12_command_module_near_USS_Hornet_%28CVS-12%29_on_24_November_1969.jpg/440px-SH-3D_of_HS-4_flies_over_Apollo_12_command_module_near_USS_Hornet_%28CVS-12%29_on_24_November_1969.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SH-3D_of_HS-4_flies_over_Apollo_12_command_module_near_USS_Hornet_(CVS-12)_on_24_November_1969.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo 12 recovery by
         <a href="/wiki/USS_Hornet_(CV-12)" title="USS Hornet (CV-12)">
          USS
          <i>
           Hornet
          </i>
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        Intrepid's
       </i>
       ascent stage was dropped (per normal procedures) after Conrad and Bean rejoined Gordon in orbit. It impacted the Moon on November 20, 1969, at
       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Apollo_12&amp;params=3.94_S_21.20_W_type:event_globe:moon&amp;title=Apollo+12+Intrepid+Module+impact">
         <span class="geo-nondefault">
          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           <span class="latitude">
            3°56′S
           </span>
           <span class="longitude">
            21°12′W
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          ﻿ / ﻿
         </span>
         <span class="geo-default">
          <span class="vcard">
           <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
            3.94°S 21.20°W
           </span>
           <span style="display:none">
            ﻿ /
            <span class="geo">
             -3.94; -21.20
            </span>
           </span>
           <span style="display:none">
            ﻿ (
            <span class="fn org">
             Apollo 12 Intrepid Module impact
            </span>
            )
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </span>
       . The seismometers the astronauts had left on the lunar surface registered the vibrations for more than an hour.
      </p>
      <p>
       The crew stayed an extra day in lunar orbit taking photographs, for a total lunar surface stay of 31 and a half hours and a total time in lunar orbit of eighty-nine hours.
      </p>
      <p>
       On the return flight to Earth after leaving lunar orbit, the crew of Apollo 12 witnessed (and photographed) a
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse" title="Solar eclipse">
        solar eclipse
       </a>
       , though this one was of the Earth eclipsing the Sun.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Splashdown">
        Splashdown
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Splashdown">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <i>
        Yankee Clipper
       </i>
       returned to Earth on November 24, 1969 at 20:58
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">
        UTC
       </a>
       (3:58pm
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone_(North_America)" title="Eastern Time Zone (North America)">
        EST
       </a>
       , 10:58am
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawaii-Aleutian_time_zone" title="Hawaii-Aleutian time zone">
        HST
       </a>
       ), in the Pacific Ocean, approximately 500 nautical miles (800 km) east of
       <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">
        American Samoa
       </a>
       . During
       <a href="/wiki/Splashdown" title="Splashdown">
        splashdown
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/16_mm_film" title="16 mm film">
        16 mm film
       </a>
       camera dislodged from storage and struck Bean in the forehead, rendering him briefly unconscious. He suffered a mild concussion and needed six stitches.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After recovery by
       <a href="/wiki/USS_Hornet_(CV-12)" title="USS Hornet (CV-12)">
        USS
        <i>
         Hornet
        </i>
       </a>
       , they were flown to
       <a href="/wiki/Pago_Pago_International_Airport" title="Pago Pago International Airport">
        Pago Pago International Airport
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Tafuna,_American_Samoa" title="Tafuna, American Samoa">
        Tafuna
       </a>
       for a reception, before being flown on a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-141" title="C-141">
        C-141
       </a>
       cargo plane to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honolulu,_Hawaii" title="Honolulu, Hawaii">
        Honolulu
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Stunts_and_mementos">
        Stunts and mementos
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Stunts and mementos">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Alan Bean smuggled a camera-shutter
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-timer" title="Self-timer">
         self-timer
        </a>
        device on to the mission with the intent of taking a photograph with himself, Pete Conrad and the
        <i>
         Surveyor 3
        </i>
        probe in the frame. As the timer was not part of their standard equipment, such an image would have thrown post-mission photo analysts into confusion over how the photo was taken. However, the self-timer was misplaced during the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">
         extra-vehicular activity
        </a>
        (EVA) and the plan was never executed.
       </li>
       <li>
        As one of the many pranks pulled during the friendly rivalry between the all-Navy prime crew and the all-Air Force backup crew, the Apollo 12 backup crew managed to insert into the astronauts' lunar checklist (attached to the wrists of Conrad's and Bean's
        <a href="/wiki/Space_suit" title="Space suit">
         space suits
        </a>
        ) reduced-sized pictures of
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">
          Playboy
         </a>
        </i>
        Playmates, surprising Conrad and Bean when they looked through the checklist flip-book during their first EVA. The
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.hq.nasa.gov/alsj/" rel="nofollow">
         Apollo Lunar Surface Journal website
        </a>
        contains a PDF file with the photocopies of their cuff checklists showing these photos.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
         <a href="#cite_note-18">
          [18]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Appearing in Conrad's checklist were
        <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Vetri" title="Victoria Vetri">
         Angela Dorian
        </a>
        , Miss September 1967 (with the caption "SEEN ANY INTERESTING HILLS &amp; VALLEYS ?") and
        <a href="/wiki/Reagan_Wilson" title="Reagan Wilson">
         Reagan Wilson
        </a>
        , Miss October 1967 ("PREFERRED TETHER PARTNER," referring to a special procedure that would require the sharing of life support resources). The photos in Bean's cuff checklist were of
        <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Myers" title="Cynthia Myers">
         Cynthia Myers
        </a>
        , Miss December 1968 ("DON'T FORGET – DESCRIBE THE PROTUBERANCES") and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leslie_Bianchini" title="Leslie Bianchini">
         Leslie Bianchini
        </a>
        , Miss January 1969 ("SURVEY – HER ACTIVITY," in
        <a href="/wiki/Pun" title="Pun">
         pun
        </a>
        of
        <i>
         Surveyor
        </i>
        ).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
         <a href="#cite_note-19">
          [19]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
         <a href="#cite_note-20">
          [20]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The backup crew who did this later flew to the Moon themselves on Apollo 15. At the back of Conrad's checklist they had also prepared two pages of complex geological terminology, added as a joke to give him the option to sound to Mission Control like he was as skilled as a professional career geologist. The third crewmember orbiting the Moon was not left out of the
        <i>
         Playboy
        </i>
        prank, as a November 1969 calendar featuring
        <a href="/wiki/DeDe_Lind" title="DeDe Lind">
         DeDe Lind
        </a>
        , Miss August 1967, had been stowed in a locker that Dick Gordon found while his crewmates were on the lunar surface. In 2011, he put this calendar up for auction. Its value was estimated by
        <a href="/wiki/RR_Auction" title="RR Auction">
         RR Auction
        </a>
        at
        <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         US$12,000–15,000
        </span>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
         <a href="#cite_note-21">
          [21]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
         <a href="#cite_note-22">
          [22]
         </a>
        </sup>
        While the Command Module Pilot calendar was in full color, the lunar checklists carried black &amp; white photocopies (although these were dramatized in
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/From_the_Earth_to_the_Moon_(miniseries)#Episodes" title="From the Earth to the Moon (miniseries)">
          From the Earth to the Moon
         </a>
        </i>
        as full color photos in the checklists).
       </li>
       <li>
        Artist
        <a href="/wiki/Forrest_Myers" title="Forrest Myers">
         Forrest "Frosty" Myers
        </a>
        claims to have installed the art piece
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Moon_Museum" title="Moon Museum">
          Moon Museum
         </a>
        </i>
        on "a leg of the Intrepid landing module with the help of an unnamed engineer at the
        <a href="/wiki/Grumman" title="Grumman">
         Grumman Corporation
        </a>
        after attempts to move the project forward through NASA's official channels were unsuccessful."
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
         <a href="#cite_note-23">
          [23]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Alan Bean left a memento on the Moon: his silver
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronaut_pin" title="Astronaut pin">
         astronaut pin
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaikin_1995_9-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Chaikin_1995-9">
          [9]
         </a>
        </sup>
        This pin signified an astronaut who completed training but had not yet flown in space; he had worn it for six years. He was to get a gold astronaut pin for successfully completing the mission after the flight and felt he wouldn't need the silver pin thereafter.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaikin_1995_9-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-Chaikin_1995-9">
          [9]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Tossing his pin into a lunar crater extended the common tradition among military pilots to ceremonially dispose of their originally awarded flight wings.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_insignia">
        Mission insignia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mission insignia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion_(SN-1).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1796" data-file-width="3554" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Apollo_12_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion_%28SN-1%29.jpg/220px-Apollo_12_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion_%28SN-1%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Apollo_12_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion_%28SN-1%29.jpg/330px-Apollo_12_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion_%28SN-1%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Apollo_12_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion_%28SN-1%29.jpg/440px-Apollo_12_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion_%28SN-1%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_12_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion_(SN-1).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo 12 space-flown silver
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_space-flown_Robbins_medallions_of_the_Apollo_missions" title="NASA space-flown Robbins medallions of the Apollo missions">
          Robbins medallion
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Apollo 12 mission patch shows the crew's navy background; all three astronauts at the time of the mission were
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">
        U.S. Navy
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Commander_(United_States)" title="Commander (United States)">
        commanders
       </a>
       . It features a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clipper_ship" title="Clipper ship">
        clipper ship
       </a>
       arriving at the Moon, representing the Command Module
       <i>
        Yankee Clipper
       </i>
       . The ship trails fire, and flies the flag of the United States. The mission name APOLLO XII and the crew names are on a wide gold border, with a small blue trim. Blue and gold are traditional U.S. Navy colors. The patch has four stars on it — one each for the three astronauts who flew the mission and one for
       <a href="/wiki/Clifton_Williams" title="Clifton Williams">
        Clifton Williams
       </a>
       , a U.S. Marine Corps aviator and astronaut who was killed on October 5, 1967, after a mechanical failure caused the controls of his
       <a href="/wiki/Northrop_T-38_Talon" title="Northrop T-38 Talon">
        T-38
       </a>
       trainer to stop responding, resulting in a crash. He trained with Conrad and Gordon as part of the backup crew for what would be the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_9" title="Apollo 9">
        Apollo 9
       </a>
       mission, and would have been assigned as Lunar Module Pilot for Apollo 12.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaikin_1995_9-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chaikin_1995-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spacecraft_location">
        Spacecraft location
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Spacecraft location">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo12_CommandModule_Hampton.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Apollo12_CommandModule_Hampton.JPG/220px-Apollo12_CommandModule_Hampton.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Apollo12_CommandModule_Hampton.JPG/330px-Apollo12_CommandModule_Hampton.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Apollo12_CommandModule_Hampton.JPG/440px-Apollo12_CommandModule_Hampton.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo12_CommandModule_Hampton.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo 12 Command Module
         <i>
          Yankee Clipper
         </i>
         on display at the
         <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Air_and_Space_Center" title="Virginia Air and Space Center">
          Virginia Air and Space Center
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">
          Hampton, Virginia
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Apollo 12 Command Module
       <i>
        Yankee Clipper
       </i>
       is on display at the
       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Air_and_Space_Center" title="Virginia Air and Space Center">
        Virginia Air and Space Center
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">
        Hampton, Virginia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2002, astronomers thought they might have discovered another moon orbiting Earth, which they designated
       <a href="/wiki/J002E3" title="J002E3">
        J002E3
       </a>
       , that turned out to be the
       <a href="/wiki/S-IVB" title="S-IVB">
        S-IVB
       </a>
       third stage of the Apollo 12 Saturn V rocket.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">

        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_Moon_Flags_Still_Standing_NASA_Lunar_Science_Institute.theora.ogv" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Series of time-lapse
         <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter">
          LRO
         </a>
         images showing a day at the Apollo 12 landing site, with the flag still standing
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Lunar Module
       <i>
        Intrepid
       </i>
       impacted the Moon November 20, 1969 at 22:17:17.7 UT (5:17 PM EST)
       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Apollo_12&amp;params=3.94_S_21.20_W_type:event_globe:moon&amp;title=Apollo+12+Intrepid+Module+impact">
         <span class="geo-nondefault">
          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           <span class="latitude">
            3°56′S
           </span>
           <span class="longitude">
            21°12′W
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
         <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          ﻿ / ﻿
         </span>
         <span class="geo-default">
          <span class="vcard">
           <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
            3.94°S 21.20°W
           </span>
           <span style="display:none">
            ﻿ /
            <span class="geo">
             -3.94; -21.20
            </span>
           </span>
           <span style="display:none">
            ﻿ (
            <span class="fn org">
             Apollo 12 Intrepid Module impact
            </span>
            )
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </span>
       . In 2009, the
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter">
        Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter
       </a>
       (LRO) photographed the Apollo 12 landing site. The
       <i>
        Intrepid
       </i>
       Lunar Module descent stage, experiment package (ALSEP),
       <i>
        Surveyor 3
       </i>
       spacecraft, and astronaut footpaths are all visible.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2011, the LRO returned to the landing site at a lower altitude to take higher resolution photographs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_LRO_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA_LRO-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Depiction_in_media">
        Depiction in media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo_12&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Depiction in media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Portions of the Apollo 12 mission are dramatized in the miniseries
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/From_the_Earth_to_the_Moon_(miniseries)" title="From the Earth to the Moon (miniseries)">
         From the Earth to the Moon
        </a>
       </i>
       episode entitled "
       <a href="/wiki/From_the_Earth_to_the_Moon_(miniseries)#Episodes" title="From the Earth to the Moon (miniseries)">
        That's All There Is
       </a>
       ". Conrad, Gordon, and Bean were portrayed by
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCrane" title="Paul McCrane">
        Paul McCrane
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tom_Verica" title="Tom Verica">
        Tom Verica
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Dave_Foley" title="Dave Foley">
        Dave Foley
       </a>
       , respectively. Conrad had been portrayed by a different actor,
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Scolari" title="Peter Scolari">
        Peter Scolari
       </a>
       , in the first episode.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
